## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and external driving. The equation of motion takes the form dv/dt = F(x, v, t)/m.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Driven Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (x**2) break symmetry — check if the system has symmetric or asymmetric behavior
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear damping/gain; terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms that are additive and independent of x and v
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x*v or x**2*v suggest nonlinear energy exchange mechanisms
- If acceleration depends explicitly on t only through trigonometric functions, the system is periodically driven; absence of t suggests autonomous dynamics
- Hardening springs correspond to x**3 terms with same sign as x; softening springs have opposite sign
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1 + c*x**2) model bounded/saturating spring forces in physical systems
- Phase-space structure: if dv_dt = f(x, v) with no explicit t dependence, the system is autonomous and can exhibit fixed points and limit cycles
